<li>Anticholinesterase agents such as pyridostigmine bromide (Mestinon) and neostigmine bromide (Prostigmin) provide symptomatic relief by increasing the relative concentration of available acetylcholine at the neuromuscular junction.</li>
<li>Dosage is increased gradually until maximal benefits are obtained.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
374</p>
<ul>
<li>Adverse effects of anticholinesterase therapy include abdominal pain, diarrhea, nausea, and increased oropharyngeal secretions.</li>
<li>Cytotoxic medications have also been used, although the precise mechanism of action in myasthenia is not fully understood.</li>
<li>Medications such as azathioprine, cyclophosphamide, and cyclosporine reduce the circulating antiacetylcholine receptor antibody titers.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
375</p>
<ul>
<li>PLASMAPHERESIS: Plasma exchange (plasmapheresis) is a technique used to treat exacerbations.</li>
<li>IV immune globulin (IVIG) has recently been shown to be nearly as effective as plasmapheresis in controlling symptom exacerbation.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
376</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-management">SURGICAL MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Thymectomy (surgical removal of the thymus gland) can produce antigen-specific immunosuppression and result in clinical improvement.</li>
<li>It can decrease or eliminate the need for medication.</li>
</ul>
<p>377</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="myasthenic-crisis">Myasthenic Crisis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#myasthenic-crisis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>A myasthenic crisis is an exacerbation of the disease process characterized by severe generalized muscle weakness and respiratory and bulbar weakness that may result in respiratory failure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Crisis may result from disease exacerbation or a specific precipitating event.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The most common precipitator is infection; others include medication change, surgery, pregnancy, and high environmental temperature.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neuromuscular respiratory failure is the critical complication of crisis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Respiratory muscle and bulbar weakness combine to cause respiratory compromise.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Neostigmine methylsulfate (PMS-Neostigmine, Prostigmin) is administered intramuscularly or intravenously until the patient is able to swallow oral anticholinesterase medications.</li>
<li>Plasmapheresis and IVIG, which reduce the antibody load, also may be used to treat myasthenic crisis</li>
</ul>
<p>380</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Respiratory support and airway protection are key interventions for the nurse caring for the patient
in crisis.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Endotracheal intubation and mechanical ventilation
may be needed.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nutritional support may be needed if the patient is intubated for a long period.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
381</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Because myasthenia gravis is a chronic disease and most patients are seen on an outpatient basis, much of the nursing care focuses on patient and family teaching.</li>
<li>Educational topics for outpatient self-care include medication management, energy conservation,
strategies to help with ocular manifestations, and prevention and management of complications</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
382</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="f09e2164">GUILLAIN-BARR SYNDROME<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#f09e2164" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Guillain-Barr syndrome is an autoimmune attack of the peripheral nerve myelin.</li>
<li>The result is acute, rapid segmental demyelination of peripheral nerves and some cranial nerves, producing ascending weakness with dyskinesia (inability to execute voluntary movements), hyporeflexia, and paresthesias (numbness).</li>
<li>In majority of the cases, there is a predisposing event, most often a respiratory or gastrointestinal infection.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
383</p>
<ul>
<li>The antecedent event usually occurs 2 weeks before symptoms begin.</li>
<li>Weakness usually begins in the legs and progresses upward for about 1 month.</li>
<li>Maximum weakness varies but usually includes neuromuscular respiratory failure and bulbar weakness.</li>
<li>The duration of the symptoms is variable: complete functional recovery may take up to 2 years</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
384</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pathophysiology">Pathophysiology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pathophysiology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Myelin is a complex substance that covers nerves, providing insulation and speeding the conduction of impulses from the cell body to the dendrites.</li>
<li>The cell that produces myelin in the peripheral nervous system is the Schwann cell.</li>
<li>In Guillain-Barr the Schwann cell is spared, allowing for remyelination in the recovery phase of the disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>385</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>muscle weakness and diminished reflexes of the lower extremities.</li>
<li>Hyporeflexia and weakness progress and may result in quadriplegia.</li>
<li>Demyelination of the nerves that innervate the diaphragm and intercostal muscles results in neuromuscular respiratory failure</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
386</p>
<ul>
<li>Cranial nerve demyelination can result in a variety of clinical manifestations.</li>
<li>Optic nerve demyelination may result in blindness.</li>
<li>Bulbar muscle weakness related to demyelination of the glossopharyngeal and vagus nerves results in an inability to swallow or clear secretions</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
387</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient presents with symmetric weakness, diminished reflexes, and upward progression of motor weakness.</li>
<li>A history of a viral illness in the previous few weeks suggests the diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
388</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Because of the possibility of rapid progression and neuromuscular respiratory failure, Guillain-Barr is a medical emergency, requiring intensive care unit management.</li>
<li>Careful assessment of changes in motor weakness and respiratory function alert the clinician to the physical and respiratory needs of the patient.</li>
<li>Respiratory therapy or mechanical ventilation may be necessary to support pulmonary function and adequate oxygenation.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
389</p>
<ul>
<li>Other interventions are aimed at preventing the complications of immobility.</li>
<li>These may include the use of anticoagulant agents and thigh-high elastic compression stockings to prevent thrombosis and pulmonary emboli.</li>
<li>Plasmapheresis and IVIG are used to directly affect the peripheral nerve myelin antibody level.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>ASSESSEMENT</li>
<li>Ongoing assessment for disease progression is critical.</li>
<li>The patient is monitored for life-threatening complications (respiratory failure, cardiac dysrhythmias, DVTs) so that appropriate interventions can be initiated.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
391</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Ineffective breathing pattern and impaired gas exchange related to rapidly progressive weakness and impending respiratory failure</li>
<li>Impaired physical mobility related to paralysis</li>
<li>Imbalanced nutrition, less than body requirements, related to inability to swallow</li>
<li>Impaired verbal communication related to cranial nerve dysfunction</li>
<li>Fear and anxiety related to loss of control and paralysis</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
392</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="potential-complications">POTENTIAL COMPLICATIONS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complications" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Respiratory failure</li>
<li>Autonomic dysfunction</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
393</p>
<p>sam
394</p>
<ul>
<li>The most common disorders of the cranial nerves are:</li>
<li>trigeminal neuralgia, a condition affecting the fifth cranial nerve, and</li>
<li>Bells palsy, caused by involvement of the seventh cranial nerve.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
395</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="trigeminal-neuralgia">TRIGEMINAL NEURALGIA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#trigeminal-neuralgia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Trigeminal neuralgia is a condition of the fifth cranial nerve characterized by paroxysms of pain in the area innervated by any of the three branches, but it most commonly occurs in the second and third branches of the trigeminal nerve.</li>
<li>The pain ends as abruptly as it starts and is described as a unilateral shooting and stabbing sensation.</li>
<li>The unilateral nature of the pain is an important diagnostic characteristic.</li>
</ul>
<p>396</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>It is associated involuntary contraction of the facial muscles can cause sudden closing of the eye or a twitch of the mouth, hence the name tic douloureux (painful twitch).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The cause is not certain, but chronic compression of the nerve at the root caused by degenerative changes and</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Vascular pressure from structural abnormalities (loop of an artery) encroaching on the trigeminal nerve, entry zone has also been suggested as a cause.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Early attacks, appearing most often in the fifth decade of life, are usually mild and brief.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Pain-free intervals may be measured in terms of minutes, hours, days, or longer.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>With advancing years, the painful episodes tend to become more frequent and agonizing.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient lives in constant fear of attacks.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
398</p>
<p> Paroxysms can occur with any stimulation of the terminals of the affected nerve branches, such as washing the face, shaving, brushing the teeth, eating, and drinking foods or drinks at extreme temperatures.</p>
<p> A draft of cold air an direct pressure against the nerve trunk may also cause pain.</p>
<p>399</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="pharmacologic-therapy">PHARMACOLOGIC THERAPY:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacologic-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Antiseizure agents, such as carbamazepine (Tegretol), relieve pain in most patients with trigeminal neuralgia by reducing the transmission of impulses at certain nerve terminals.</li>
<li>Carbamazepine is taken with meals to minimize its side effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
400</p>
<ul>
<li>Gabapentin (Neurontin) and baclofen are also used if the patient is not responding to carbamazepine.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
401</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-management">SURGICAL MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>When these methods fail to relieve pain, a number of surgical options are available.</li>
<li>The choice of procedure depends on the patient's preference and health status.</li>
<li>The surgical procedures are;</li>
<li>Microvascular Decompression of the Trigeminal Nerve</li>
<li>Percutaneous Radiofrequency Trigeminal Gangliolysis.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
402</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>It entails prevention of pain by teaching patient to prevent the aggravating factors.</li>
<li>Postoperative neurologic assessments are conducted to evaluate the patient for facial motor and sensory deficits in each of the three branches of the trigeminal nerve</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
403</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bell-s-palsy">BELL'S PALSY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bell-s-palsy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Bell's palsy (facial paralysis) is due to unilateral inflammation of the seventh cranial nerve, which results in weakness or paralysis of the facial muscles on the affected side.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The cause is unknown, although possible causes may include vascular ischemia, viral disease (herpes simplex, herpes zoster), autoimmune disease, or a combination of all of these factors.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
404</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The inflamed, edematous nerve becomes compressed to the point of damage, or its nutrient vessel is occluded, producing ischemic necrosis of the nerve.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is distortion of the face from paralysis of the facial muscles; increased lacrimation (tearing); and painful sensations in the face, behind the ear, and in the eye.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The patient may experience speech difficulties and may be unable to eat on the affected side because of weakness or paralysis of the facial muscles.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>405</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="management">Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The objectives of treatment are to maintain the muscle tone of the face and to prevent or minimize denervation.</li>
<li>The patient should be reassured that no stroke has occurred and that spontaneous recovery occurs within 3 to 5 weeks.</li>
<li>Corticosteroid therapy (prednisone) may be prescribed to reduce inflammation and edema; this reduces vascular compression and permits restoration of blood circulation to the nerve.</li>
</ul>
<p> Facial pain is controlled with analgesic agents
 Although most patients recover with conservative treatment, surgical exploration of the facial nerve may be indicated in patients who are suspected of having a tumor or for surgical decompression of the facial nerve and for surgical treatment of a paralyzed face.</p>
<p>sam
407</p>
<p>sam
408</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="objectives">OBJECTIVES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>At the end of the lesson the learner should be able to:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Identify the pathophysiologic processes responsible for oncologic disorders.</li>
<li>Describe brain and spinal cord tumors: their classification, clinical manifestations, diagnosis, and medical and nursing management.</li>
<li>Use the nursing process as a framework for care of patients with cerebral metastases</li>
</ol>
<p>409</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="primary-brain-tumors">PRIMARY BRAIN TUMORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-brain-tumors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A brain tumor is a localized intracranial lesion that occupies space within the skull.</li>
<li>Tumors usually grow as a spherical mass, but they can grow diffusely and infiltrate tissue.</li>
<li>The effects of neoplasms occur from the compression and infiltration of tissue.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
410</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-variety-of-physiologic-changes">A variety of physiologic changes<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-variety-of-physiologic-changes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Increased intracranial pressure (ICP) and cerebral edema</li>
<li>Seizure activity and focal neurologic signs</li>
<li>Hydrocephalus</li>
<li>Altered pituitary function</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
411</p>
<p> Primary brain tumors originate from cells and structures within the brain.</p>
<p> Secondary, or metastatic, brain tumors develop from structures outside the brain and occur in 20% to 40% of all patients with cancer</p>
<p>sam
412</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="brain-tumors-may-be-classified-into-several-groups">Brain tumors may be classified into several groups:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#brain-tumors-may-be-classified-into-several-groups" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Those arising from the coverings of the brain (dural meningioma)</li>
<li>Those developing in or on the cranial nerves (eg, acoustic neuroma),</li>
<li>Those originating within brain tissue (eg, gliomas), and metastatic lesions originating elsewhere in the body.</li>
<li>Tumors of the pituitary and pineal glands and of cerebral blood vessels are also types of brain tumors.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
413</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="gliomas">GLIOMAS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#gliomas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Infiltrate any portion of the brain; most common type of brain tumor.</li>
<li>ANGIOMAS: These are masses composed largely of abnormal blood vessels are found either in or on the surface of the brain</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
414</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Brain tumors can produce either focal or generalized neurologic signs and symptoms.</li>
<li>Generalized symptoms reflect increased ICP, and the most common focal or specific signs and symptoms result from tumors interfering with functions in specific brain regions.</li>
<li>Review signs and symptoms of increased ICP.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="localized-symptoms">LOCALIZED SYMPTOMS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#localized-symptoms" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Hemiparesis,</li>
<li>Seizures,</li>
<li>Mental status changes</li>
<li>such as sensory and motor abnormalities,</li>
<li>visual alterations,</li>
<li>Alterations in cognition, and language disturbances such as aphasia.</li>
</ul>
<p>416</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The history of the illness and the manner and time frame in which the symptoms evolved are key components in the diagnosis of brain tumors.</li>
<li>A neurologic examination indicates the areas of the CNS involved.</li>
<li>Computed tomography (CT) scans gives specific information concerning the number, size, and density of the lesions.</li>
<li>MRI also helps in diagnosis.</li>
</ul>
<p>417</p>
<ul>
<li>Cerebral angiography provides visualization of cerebral blood vessels and can localize most cerebral tumors.</li>
<li>An electroencephalogram (EEG) can detect an abnormal brain wave in regions occupied by a tumor and is used to evaluate temporal lobe seizures</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
418</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A variety of medical treatment modalities, including chemotherapy and external-beam radiation therapy, are used alone or in combination with surgical resection.</li>
<li>Radiation therapy, the cornerstone of treatment of many brain tumors, decreases the incidence of recurrence of incompletely resected tumors.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam</p>
<ul>
<li>Corticosteroids may be used before and after treatment to reduce cerebral edema and promote a smoother, more rapid recovery.</li>
</ul>
<p>SURGICAL MANAGEMENT:</p>
<ul>
<li>The objective of surgical management is to remove or destroy the entire tumor without increasing the neurologic deficit (paralysis, blindness) or to relieve symptoms by partial removal (decompression).</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
420</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The patient with a brain tumor may be at an increased risk for aspiration due to cranial nerve dysfunction.</li>
<li>Preoperatively, the gag reflex and ability to swallow are evaluated.</li>
<li>In patients with diminished gag response, care includes teaching the patient to direct food and fluids toward the unaffected side, having the patient sit upright to eat, offering a semisoft diet, and having suction readily available.</li>
</ul>
<p>421</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The nurse performs neurologic checks, monitors vital signs, maintains a neurologic flow chart, spaces nursing interventions to prevent rapid increase in ICP, and reorients the patient when necessary to person, time, and place.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Patients with changes in cognition caused by the lesion require frequent reorientation.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
422</p>
<ul>
<li>Motor function is checked at intervals because specific motor deficits may occur, depending on the tumors location.</li>
<li>Sensory disturbances are assessed. Speech is evaluated.</li>
<li>Eye movement and pupillary size and reaction may be affected by cranial nerve involvement.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
423</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cerebral-metastases">CEREBRAL METASTASES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cerebral-metastases" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A significant number of patients with cancer experience neurologic deficits caused by metastasis to the brain.</li>
<li>Neurologic signs and symptoms include headache, gait disturbances, visual impairment, personality changes, altered mentation (memory loss and confusion), focal weakness, paralysis, aphasia, and seizures.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
424</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The treatment of metastatic brain cancer is palliative and involves eliminating or reducing serious symptoms.</li>
<li>The therapeutic approach includes radiation therapy, surgery (usually for a single intracranial metastasis), and chemotherapy.</li>
<li>More often some combination of these treatments is the optimal method.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
425</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pharmacologic-therapy">PHARMACOLOGIC THERAPY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pharmacologic-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Corticosteroids are useful in relieving headache and alterations in level of consciousness.</li>
<li>It is thought that corticosteroids (dexamethasone, prednisone) reduce inflammation around the metastatic deposits and decrease the edema surrounding them.</li>
<li>Other medications used include osmotic agents (mannitol) to decrease the fluid content of the brain.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
426</p>
<ul>
<li>Antiseizure agents (eg, phenytoin) are used to prevent and treat seizures.</li>
<li>Venous thromboembolic events, such as deep vein thrombosis (DVT) and pulmonary embolism (PE), occur in about 15% of patients and are associated with significant morbidity.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
427</p>
<ul>
<li>If the patient has severe pain, morphine can be infused into the epidural or subarachnoid space through a spinal needle and a catheter as near as possible to the spinal segment where the pain is projected.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
428</p>
<p>sam
429</p>
<ul>
<li>Neurologic disorders of the central and peripheral nervous system that are degenerative in nature include:</li>
<li>Parkinsons disease</li>
<li>Huntingtons disease</li>
<li>Alzheimers disease</li>
<li>Amyotrophic lateral sclerosis,</li>
<li>muscular dystrophies, and</li>
<li>Degenerative disc disease.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="parkinson-s-disease">PARKINSON'S DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#parkinson-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Parkinson's disease is a slowly progressing neurologic movement disorder that eventually leads to disability.</li>
<li>The degenerative or idiopathic form is the most common; there is also a secondary form with a known or suspected cause.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
431</p>
<ul>
<li>Research suggests several causative factors, including genetics, atherosclerosis, excessive accumulation of oxygen free radicals, viral infections, head trauma, chronic antipsychotic medication use, and some environmental exposures.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
432</p>
<ul>
<li>Parkinsonian symptoms usually first appear in the fifth decade of life; however, cases have been diagnosed at the age of 30 years.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
433</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Parkinson's disease has a gradual onset and symptoms progress slowly over a chronic, prolonged course.</li>
<li>The three cardinal signs are tremor, rigidity, and bradykinesia (abnormally slow movements).</li>
<li>Other features include hypokinesia, gait disturbances, and postural instability.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
434</p>
<ul>
<li>Psychiatric changes are often interrelated and may be predictive of one another.</li>
<li>They include depression, dementia (progressive mental deterioration), sleep disturbances, and hallucinations.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
435</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Currently, the disease is diagnosed clinically from the patients history and the presence of two of the three cardinal manifestations: tremor, muscle rigidity, and bradykinesia.</li>
<li>Laboratory tests and imaging studies are not helpful in the diagnosis of Parkinsons disease, although PET scanning has been used in evaluating levodopa (precursor of dopamine) uptake and conversion to dopamine in the corpus striatum</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
436</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Treatment is directed at controlling symptoms and maintaining functional independence because there are no medical or surgical approaches that prevent disease progression.</li>
<li>Antiparkinsonian Medications. Levodopa (Dopar, Larodopa) is the most effective agent and the mainstay of treatment.</li>
<li>Levodopa is usually given in combination with carbidopa (Sinemet), an inhibitor that helps to maximize the beneficial effects of levodopa by preventing its breakdown outside the brain and reducing its adverse effects.</li>
</ul>
<p>437</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Anticholinergic Therapy. Anticholinergic agents (trihexyphenidyl, cycrimine, procyclidine, biperiden, and benztropine mesylate) are effective in controlling tremor and rigidity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They may be used in combination with levodopa.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They counteract the action of the neurotransmitter acetylcholine.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
438</p>
<ul>
<li>Dopamine Agonists. Bromocriptine mesylate and pergolide (ergot derivatives) are dopamine receptor agonists and are useful in postponing the initiation of carbidopa or levodopa therapy.</li>
<li>Dopamine agonists are often added to the medication regimen when carbidopa or levodopa loses effectiveness</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
439</p>
<ul>
<li>Antidepressants. Tricyclic antidepressants may be prescribed to alleviate the depression that is so common in Parkinson's disease.</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>SURGICAL MANAGEMENT:</strong></p>
<ul>
<li>The limitations of levodopa therapy, improvements in stereotactic surgery, and new approaches in transplantation have renewed interest in the surgical treatment of Parkinson's disease.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
440</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Assessment</li>
<li>Assessment focuses on how the disease has affected the patient's activities of daily living and functional abilities.</li>
<li>Patients are observed for degree of disability and the functional changes that occur throughout the day, such as responses to medication.</li>
<li>Nearly every patient with a movement disorder has some functional alteration and may have some type of behavioral dysfunction.</li>
</ul>
<p>441</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Impaired physical mobility related to muscle rigidity and motor weakness</li>
<li>Self-care deficits (feeding, dressing, hygiene, and toileting) related to tremor and motor disturbance</li>
<li>Constipation related to medication and reduced activity</li>
<li>Imbalanced nutrition, less than body requirements, related to tremor, slowness in eating, difficulty in chewing and swallowing.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="huntington-s-disease">HUNTINGTON'S DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#huntington-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Huntington's disease is a chronic, progressive, hereditary disease of the nervous system that results in progressive involuntary choreiform movement and dementia.</li>
<li>It affects men and women of all races.</li>
<li>The basic pathology involves premature death of cells in the striatum (caudate and putamen) of the basal ganglia, the region deep within the brain involved in the control of movement.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
443</p>
<ul>
<li>There is also loss of cells in the cortex, the region of the brain associated with thinking, memory, perception, and judgment, and in the cerebellum, the area that coordinates voluntary muscle activity.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The most prominent clinical features of the disease are abnormal involuntary movements (chorea), intellectual decline, and, often, emotional disturbance. As the disease progresses, a constant writhing, twisting, uncontrollable movement may involve the entire body.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Although no treatment halts or reverses the underlying process, several methods of management have fairly good palliative results.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="alzheimer-s-disease">ALZHEIMER'S DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alzheimer-s-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Alzheimers disease, or senile dementia of the Alzheimers type, is a chronic, progressive, and degenerative brain disorder accompanied by profound effects on memory, cognition, and ability for self-care.</li>
<li>About 10% of the population older than age 65 are affected, and the prevalence reaches 47% by age 85</li>
<li>Management is supportive care.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
446</p>
<ul>
<li>Read and make notes on other degenerative disorders.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
447</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="seizure-disorders">SEIZURE DISORDERS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#seizure-disorders" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="seizures">SEIZURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#seizures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Seizures are episodes of abnormal motor, sensory, autonomic, or psychic activity (or a combination of these) resulting from sudden excessive discharge from cerebral neurons.</li>
<li>A part or all of the brain may be involved.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
448</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="classification-of-seizures">CLASSIFICATION OF SEIZURES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#classification-of-seizures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are two main classification of seizures: partial seizures that begin in one part of the brain, and generalized seizures that involve electrical discharges in the whole brain.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
449</p>
<ul>
<li>Partial seizures are further divided into simple partial seizures and Complex partial seizures.</li>
<li>Generalised seizures are further classified into:</li>
<li>Tonic-clonic seizures</li>
<li>Tonic seizures</li>
<li>Clonic seizures</li>
<li>Absence seizures</li>
<li>Myoclonic seizures</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
450</p>
<p>451
sam</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The underlying cause is an electrical disturbance in the nerve cells in one section of the brain, causing them to emit abnormal, recurring, uncontrolled electrical discharges.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The characteristic seizure is a manifestation of this excessive neuronal discharge.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There may be associated loss of consciousness, excess movement or loss of muscle tone or movement, and disturbances of behavior, mood, sensation, and perception.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="causes">CAUSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#causes" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Causes of seizures can be grouped into two:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Idiopathic (genetic, developmental defects)</li>
<li>Acquired seizures are due to hypoxemia of any cause, including vascular insufficiency, fever (childhood), head injury, hypertension, central nervous system infections, metabolic and toxic conditions, brain tumor, drug and alcohol</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The type of movements in the part of the body involved</li>
<li>Incontinence of urine or stool</li>
<li>Duration of each phase of the seizure</li>
<li>Unconsciousness, if present, and its duration</li>
<li>Any obvious paralysis or weakness of arms or legs after the seizure</li>
<li>Inability to speak after the seizure</li>
<li>Movements at the end of the seizure</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-epilepsies">THE EPILEPSIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-epilepsies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Epilepsy is a group of syndromes characterized by recurring seizures.</li>
<li>Epileptic syndromes are classified by specific patterns of clinical features, including age of onset, family history, and seizure type.</li>
<li>Types of epilepsies are differentiated by how the seizure activity manifests, the most common syndromes being those with generalized seizures and those with partial-onset seizures.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
454</p>
<ul>
<li>Epilepsy can be primary (idiopathic) or secondary, when the cause is known and the epilepsy is a symptom of another underlying condition such as a brain tumor.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
455</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="clinical-manifestations">Clinical Manifestations<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#clinical-manifestations" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Depending on the location of the discharging neurons, seizures may range from a simple staring episode to prolonged convulsive movements with loss of consciousness.</li>
<li>The initial pattern of the seizures indicates the region of the brain in which the seizure originates.</li>
<li>In simple partial seizures, only a finger or hand may shake, or the mouth may jerk uncontrollably.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
456</p>
<ul>
<li>In complex partial seizures, the person either remains motionless or moves automatically but inappropriately for time and place, or may experience excessive emotions of fear, anger, or irritability.</li>
<li>There is involvement of more than one part of the brain.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="generalized-seizures">Generalized seizures<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#generalized-seizures" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Previously referred to as grand mal seizures, involve both hemispheres of the brain, causing both sides of the body to react.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
458</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="stages-of-grand-mal-seizure">STAGES OF GRAND MAL SEIZURE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#stages-of-grand-mal-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Prodrome stage: It occurs days or hours before the seizure activity. It is characterized by irritability or hyperactivity etc.</li>
<li>Aura (warning)stage: It is characterised by certain unusual feelings such as peculiar sensation, funny smell, feeling nauseated, abdominal discomfort (gastric secretions) and flashing light.</li>
</ol>
<p>sam
459</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Tonic stage: It usually lasts about 10 to 20 seconds.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>All muscles become rigid, eyelids open, eyes look up and respiration stops temporarily resulting in cyanosis.</li>
<li>The tongue is bitten causing bleeding, which can be seen from the mouth.</li>
</ul>
<ol start="4">
<li>Clonic stage: It usually lasts about 30 seconds.</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>It begins with muscle relaxation, which completely interrupts tonic muscle contraction.</li>
<li>There are brief violent muscle spasms of the whole body, frothing of the mouth and incontinence of urine and sometimes faeces as well.</li>
</ul>
<p>460</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>
<p>Ictal phase: The patient goes into deep coma for minutes or hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Post ictal stage: (after the seizure). This is recovery stage, the patient starts regaining consciousness.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>The patient is often confused and hard to arouse and may sleep for hours.</li>
<li>Many patients complain of headache, sore muscles, fatigue, and depression</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
461</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="assessment-and-diagnostic-findings">Assessment and Diagnostic Findings<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment-and-diagnostic-findings" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A developmental history is taken, including events of pregnancy and childbirth, to seek evidence of preexisting injury.</li>
<li>The patient is also questioned about illnesses or head injuries that may have affected the brain.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="diagnostic-tests-include">DIAGNOSTIC TESTS INCLUDE:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diagnostic-tests-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>MRI is used to detect lesions in the brain and focal abnormalities.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
462</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The electroencephalogram (EEG) furnishes diagnostic evidence in a substantial proportion of patients with epilepsy and aids in classifying the type of seizure.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Single photon emission computed tomography (SPECT) is an additional tool sometimes used in the diagnostic workup.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
463</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Many medications are available to control seizures, although the mechanisms of their actions are still unknown.</li>
<li>The objective is to achieve seizure control with minimal side effects.</li>
<li>Medication therapy controls rather than cures seizures.</li>
<li>Treatment is usually started with a single medication.</li>
<li>The dose and the rate at which the dosage is increased depend on the occurrence of side effects</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
464</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="antiseizure-drugs">ANTISEIZURE DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antiseizure-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>carbamazepine (Tegretol)</li>
<li>clonazepam (Klonopin)</li>
<li>ethosuximide (Zarontin)</li>
<li>felbamate (Felbatol)</li>
<li>gabapentin (Neurotonin)</li>
<li>lamotrigine (Lamictal)</li>
<li>levetiracetam (Keppra)</li>
<li>oxacarbazepine (Trileptal)</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
465</p>
<ul>
<li>phenobarbital (Luminal)</li>
<li>phenytoin (Dilantin)</li>
<li>primidone (Mysoline)</li>
<li>tiagabine (Gabitril)</li>
<li>topiramate (Topamax)</li>
<li>valproate (Depakote, Depakene)</li>
<li>zonisamide (Zonegran, Excegran</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
466</p>
<ul>
<li>Review the pharmacology of anti seizure drugs.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
467</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="side-effects-of-ant-iseizure-drugs">SIDE EFFECTS OF ANT ISEIZURE DRUGS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#side-effects-of-ant-iseizure-drugs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Side effects of antiseizure agents may be divided into three groups:
(1) idiosyncratic or allergic disorders, which present primarily as skin reactions;
(2) acute toxicity, which may occur when the medication is initially prescribed; or
(3) chronic toxicity, which occurs late in the course of therapy.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
468</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="surgical-management">SURGICAL MANAGEMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#surgical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Surgery is indicated for patients whose epilepsy results from intracranial tumors, abscess, cysts, or vascular anomalies.</li>
<li>Some patients have intractable seizure disorders that do not respond to medication.</li>
</ul>
<p>469</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>There may be a focal atrophic process secondary to trauma, inflammation, stroke, or anoxia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If the seizures originate in a reasonably well-circumscribed area of the brain that can be excised without producing significant neurologic deficits, the removal of the area generating the seizures may produce long-term control and improvement.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
470</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-assessment-during-a-seizure">Nursing Assessment During a Seizure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-assessment-during-a-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A major responsibility of the nurse is to observe and record the sequence of symptoms.</li>
<li>The nature of the seizure usually indicates the type of treatment that is required.</li>
<li>The nurse assesses for the following:</li>
<li>The circumstances before the seizure (visual, auditory, or olfactory stimuli, tactile stimuli, etc)</li>
<li>The occurrence of an aura (visual, auditory, or olfactory)</li>
<li>The first thing the patient does in a seizure</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
471</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-during-a-seizure">Nursing Care During a Seizure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-during-a-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Provide privacy and protect the patient from curious on-lookers.</li>
<li>(The patient who has an aura [warning of an impending seizure]</li>
<li>may have time to seek a safe, private place.)</li>
<li>Ease the patient to the floor, if possible.</li>
<li>Protect the head with a pad to prevent injury (from striking a hard surface).</li>
<li>Loosen constrictive clothing.</li>
<li>Push aside any furniture that may injure the patient during the seizure.</li>
</ul>
<p>472</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>If the patient is in bed, remove pillows and raise side rails.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If an aura precedes the seizure, insert an oral airway to reduce the possibility of the tongue or cheek being bitten.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>NB: Do not attempt to pry open jaws that are clenched in a spasm to insert anything. Broken teeth and injury to the lips and tongue may result from such an action.</p>
<ul>
<li>No attempt should be made to restrain the patient during the seizure because muscular contractions are strong and restraint can produce injury.</li>
</ul>
<p>473</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>If possible, place the patient on one side with head flexed forward, which allows the tongue to fall forward and facilitates drainage of saliva and mucus.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If suction is available, use it if necessary to clear secretions.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
474</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-care-after-the-seizure">Nursing Care After the Seizure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-care-after-the-seizure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Keep the patient on one side to prevent aspiration. Make sure the airway is patent.</li>
<li>There is usually a period of confusion after a grand mal seizure.</li>
<li>A short apneic period may occur during or immediately after a generalized seizure.</li>
<li>The patient, on awakening, should be reoriented to the environment.</li>
<li>If the patient becomes agitated after a seizure (postictal), use calm persuasion and gentle restraint.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
475</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-process">NURSING PROCESS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-process" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="assessment">ASSESSMENT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#assessment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>The nurse elicits information about the seizure history.</li>
<li>The patient is asked about the factors or events that may precipitate the seizures.</li>
<li>The nurse determines if the patient has an aura (a premonitory or warning sensation) before an epileptic seizure, which may indicate the origin of the seizure.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
476</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-diagnoses">NURSING DIAGNOSES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-diagnoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Risk for injury related to seizure activity</li>
<li>Fear related to the possibility of seizures</li>
<li>Ineffective individual coping related to stresses imposed by epilepsy</li>
<li>Deficient knowledge related to epilepsy and its control</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
477</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="potential-complication">POTENTIAL COMPLICATION<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#potential-complication" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Status epilepticus</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
478</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="status-epilepticus">STATUS EPILEPTICUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#status-epilepticus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Status epilepticus (acute prolonged seizure activity) is a series of generalized seizures that occur without full recovery of consciousness between attacks.</li>
<li>It is considered a medical emergency.</li>
<li>Status epilepticus produces cumulative effects.</li>
<li>Vigorous muscular contractions impose a heavy metabolic demand and can interfere with respirations.</li>
<li>There is some respiratory arrest at the height of each seizure that produces venous congestion and hypoxia of the brain.</li>
</ul>
<p>479</p>
<ul>
<li>Repeated episodes of cerebral anoxia and edema may lead to irreversible and fatal brain damage.</li>
<li>Factors that precipitate status epilepticus include withdrawal of antiseizure medication, fever, and concurrent infection.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="medical-management">Medical Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#medical-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The goals of treatment are to stop the seizures as quickly as possible, to ensure adequate cerebral oxygenation, and to maintain the patient in a seizure-free state.</li>
<li>An airway and adequate oxygenation are established.</li>
<li>If the patient remains unconscious and unresponsive, a cuffed endotracheal tube is inserted.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
481</p>
<ul>
<li>Intravenous diazepam (Valium), or lorazepam is given slowly in an attempt to halt seizures immediately.</li>
<li>Other medications (phenytoin, phenobarbital) are given later to maintain a seizure-free state.</li>
<li>EEG monitoring may be useful in determining the nature of the seizure activity.</li>
<li>Vital signs and neurologic signs are monitored on a continuing basis.</li>
<li>An intravenous infusion of dextrose is given if the seizure is due to hypoglycemia.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
482</p>
<ul>
<li>If initial treatment is unsuccessful, general anesthesia with a short-acting barbiturate may be used.</li>
</ul>
<p>sam
483</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nursing-management">Nursing Management<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nursing-management" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>The nurse initiates ongoing assessment and monitoring of respiratory and cardiac function because of the risk for delayed depression of respiration and blood pressure secondary to administration of antiseizure medications and sedatives to halt the seizures.</li>
